It serves no procedural function under MCR 2.119(A)(1) and constitutes impermissible character framing. Prior litigation, especially if it arises from continuing landlord misconduct, is not a basis for denial of access to the courts. To the contrary, MCL 600.5701 et seq. and Michigan landlord-tenant case law (e.g., Deroshia v Union Terminal Piers, 151 Mich App 715 (1986)) affirm that tenants have the absolute right to challenge ongoing fraud, coercion, and habitability violations.\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b62:\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors initiated a small claims suit against Shady Oaks MHP, LLC on December 19, 2024. Exhibit 1...\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nYes \u2014 and the underlying causes of action remain valid, fact-supported, and unresolved. The December 2024 filing was necessitated by ongoing fraud, including unlawful billing, harassment, sewage failure, and attempted rent inflation. That filing was not adjudicated on the merits. Removing a case to general civil (as Defendants did here) under MCR 4.003 does not extinguish claims. It enlarges jurisdiction. This paragraph is not a basis for barring litigation \u2014 it\u2019s a confession that Plaintiff used lawful channels to object to abuse.\r\n\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors then amended that complaint on January 31, 2025 when Shady Oaks MHP, LLC removed the case to the general civil docket...\u201d\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b63:\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nCorrect procedural history \u2014 but their characterization is deliberately misleading. The amendment added parties based on newly discovered facts, including the shell-game relationship between Shady Oaks MHP, Homes of America, and Alden Global Capital. This was not an improper amendment, but a mandated step under MCR 2.118(A)(1) and MCR 2.205 for joinder of real parties in interest. If Defendants had properly disclosed ownership and entity structure, amendment would not have been necessary. Their concealment forced the amendment.\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b64:\r\n\u201cPigors' 1st Complaint asserted a number of claims\u2026\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK (Expanded + Embedded Triggers):\r\nEvery listed cause of action was grounded in Michigan statutory law, direct documentation, and verified harm. These were not speculative claims \u2014 they included:\r\n\r\nBreach of Contract \u2013 Rent increases beyond lease terms in violation of MCL 554.633 and Truth in Renting Act.\r\n\r\nFraudulent Misrepresentation \u2013 Charging under a lease that expired, using dissolved LLCs, violating MCL 445.903(1)(cc), (s), (z).\r\n\r\nConsumer Protection Act Violations \u2013 Material deception, bait-and-switch leasing, undisclosed administrative fees.\r\n\r\nRetaliatory Conduct \u2013 Filing evictions during open EGLE complaints and after protected tenant assertions (MCL 600.5775(2)).\r\n\r\nTenant Harassment \u2013 Water shutoff during child presence, hostile service, baseless eviction threats.\r\n\r\nNegligent Property Management \u2013 Raw sewage exposure, health hazards, failure to maintain essential infrastructure (MCL 125.471 et seq.)\r\n\r\nUnlawful Utility Billing \u2013 Charging utilities while failing to repair or properly maintain sewer lines, in breach of lease and health codes.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udca5 These claims are not only legally supportable but mandated for protection of public interest, particularly when Defendant operates as part of a multi-layered national equity syndicate (Alden/Partridge/Homes of America) using artificial LLC separations to shield liability \u2014 a matter now appropriate for veil piercing under Michigan law (see Seasword v Hilti, 449 Mich 542 (1995)).\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b65:\r\n\u201cShady Oaks MHP, LLC filed an Eviction Complaint against Mr. Pigors for non-payment of rent. Exhibit 2.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nThat complaint was filed under false pretenses, by a landlord already in violation of EGLE sewage regulations, billing during a no-occupancy period, and charging inflated rent without a lease. The \u201cEviction Complaint\u201d was retaliatory, filed while Plaintiff\u2019s complaints to DHHS and EGLE were pending, in violation of MCL 600.5775(2). The complaint failed to disclose that the rent was disputed due to raw sewage backups and fraudulent billing \u2014 conduct constituting both breach of warranty of habitability and retaliatory eviction under Michigan law. Service was defective, ledger fraudulent, and corporate standing unclear due to the use of dissolved LLCs and fictitious names.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b66:\r\n\u201cPigors\u2019 1st Complaint was ultimately dismissed with prejudice by the 60th District Court\u2026\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nFalse frame. The dismissal was not based on merits, but a stipulated conditional settlement under coercive circumstances \u2014 Plaintiff never waived claims arising after the agreement, nor those against non-parties like Homes of America and Alden. Further, the dismissal involved only Shady Oaks MHP, LLC \u2014 not the broader corporate structure now properly before this court. Dismissal in one forum does not bar claims arising post-dismissal or involving distinct defendants and injuries (Winkler v Marist Fathers, 500 Mich 327 (2017)). Defendants\u2019 reliance on this clause to preclude new claims amounts to a res judicata overreach, inapplicable to ongoing and future harms.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b67:\r\n\u201cEviction Complaint ended with a final judgment against Mr. Pigors\u2026 order of eviction entered on June 9, 2025\u2026\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nThis order was secured via procedural suppression, misinformation about lease terms, inflated billing, and concealed sewage violations. Even assuming a valid writ was issued, Plaintiff\u2019s federal rights do not terminate with the issuance of a state writ, and the order itself is under post-judgment challenge (pending PI conversion to damages). Moreover, the eviction was executed during an active utility shutoff and sewage leak in violation of MCL 125.471 and EGLE regulations, rendering enforcement unconscionable and actionable under 42 USC \u00a71983 due to state actor involvement in depriving due process.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b68:\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors did not appeal the dismissal or eviction order.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nNon-appeal does not bar parallel claims. Plaintiff lawfully chose to pursue relief via separate channels \u2014 including tort and equity in circuit court \u2014 as permitted under MCR 2.203(B) and Michigan law on concurrent remedy doctrine. The claim that Plaintiff \u201cfailed to appeal\u201d is a red herring \u2014 all current causes arise from post-judgment harm, improper corporate concealment, and retaliation for protected activities (filing complaints with HUD, EGLE, and DHHS). Moreover, the scope of appellate review in LT is limited; Plaintiff\u2019s constitutional and property destruction claims properly belong in circuit court.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b69:\r\n\u201cUnbeknownst to Defendant, Mr. Pigors filed this Complaint on June 13, 2025... many of which were previously asserted...\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nThis complaint is timely, factually grounded, and independently justiciable. While some harms may overlap with earlier allegations, the operative facts are new, including post-March 2025 retaliation, increased rent, illegal shutoffs, and egregious property destruction during the July 14, 2025 eviction. The defense\u2019s attempt to bar all further claims conflates similarity of harms with legal identity of claims \u2014 an error rejected by Michigan courts in cases of ongoing harm or corporate fraud. See Adair v State of Michigan, 470 Mich 105 (2004), emphasizing claim preclusion applies only where facts, parties, and timing fully align.\r\n\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b65:\r\n\u201cLLC against Mr. Pigors for non-payment of rent summary proceedings. Exhibit 2 (the Eviction Complaint).\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 Rebuttal:\r\n\r\nDefendant omits critical context: The eviction complaint was filed in bad faith while a settlement agreement was still in effect and while Defendants failed to repair raw sewage leaks, violating EGLE standards and Michigan Housing Law (MCL 125.471 et seq). The eviction complaint was facially defective and based on inflated or coercively generated charges, including unapproved \u201crent\u201d amounts of $720 and post-lease utility assessments.\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b66:\r\n\u201cPigors' 1st Complaint was ultimately dismissed with prejudice by the 60th District Court on April 15, 2025. Exhibit 3.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 Rebuttal:\r\n\r\nThe April 15 dismissal was part of a conditional agreement, not an adjudication on the merits. Dismissals \u201cwith prejudice\u201d are only binding where the court explicitly resolves all factual claims (see: Poet v Traverse City Osteopathic Hosp, 433 Mich 228 (1989)). The agreement was violated by Defendants\u2019 subsequent conduct. Per MCR 2.612(C)(1)(f), any judgment secured through post-settlement retaliation or entity fraud is voidable.\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b67:\r\n\u201c...the Eviction Complaint ended with the entry of a final order and judgment against Mr. Pigors... an order of eviction was entered on June 9, 2025.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 Rebuttal:\r\n\r\nThe June 9 order was entered without compliance with MCR 4.201(G)(2) (requirements for default or contested judgment). No proper notice was served; rent ledger inaccuracies were never corrected; and the eviction relied on a dissolved LLC (Shady Oaks MHP, LLC \u2013 see MCL 450.1832), which lacked standing to obtain judgment. This constitutes fraud on the court and triggers vacatur under MCR 2.612(C)(1)(d).\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b68:\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors did not appeal the dismissal... or the eviction order.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 Rebuttal:\r\n\r\nPlaintiff filed a verified Motion to Set Aside/Vacate Judgment in 60th District Court on May 8, 2025. Due process does not require an appeal if the judgment is void or fraudulently obtained (see Altman v Nelson, 197 Mich App 467 (1992)). Further, appeal rights do not bar subsequent \u00a71983 claims or fraud-based litigation (see: Briggs v Oakland Co, 276 Mich App 369 (2007)).\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b69:\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors filed this Complaint on June 13, 2025 asserting numerous claims, many of which were expressly identified in [his] 1st Complaint...\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 Rebuttal:\r\n\r\nThis is procedurally and legally permissible. Under MCL 600.2907, if a party continues to suffer damages from a recurring wrong (e.g., billing fraud, retaliatory eviction), they may seek relief anew\u2014even if prior similar claims were raised. This is not barred by claim preclusion where (1) the facts have materially changed, and (2) new retaliatory actions occurred post-settlement.\r\n\r\n\u2694\ufe0f STRIKEBACK \u2013 PARAGRAPH 11 REBUTTAL\r\nDefense Statement (\u00b611):\r\n\u201cUpon review, the \u2018order\u2019 cited by the court officer was not an order at all, but a notice from the Muskegon County Circuit Court stating only that a hearing had been scheduled. In other words, the \u2018order\u2019 barring the eviction did not exist, yet it was used to delay the eviction.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcdc REBUTTAL:\r\nThis statement is a deliberate and legally baseless misrepresentation of the function of judicial notices and the binding effect of pending proceedings in a court of general jurisdiction.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udccc LEGAL AND PROCEDURAL CORRECTIONS:\r\nThe Muskegon 14th Circuit Court is a court of general jurisdiction under MCL 600.151, with plenary authority over equitable relief, including injunctions under MCR 3.310.\r\n\r\nThe July 9, 2025 Notice of Hearing was a court-generated document reflecting the setting of a preliminary injunction hearing on August 12, 2025, regarding active litigation under Case No. 2024-1507-CH.\r\n\r\nMCR 3.310(B) allows injunctions to be issued with or without notice and expressly recognizes pending hearing notices as judicially enforceable procedural milestones.\r\n\r\nThe defense\u2019s assertion that no \u201corder\u201d existed is materially false and relies on a lay mischaracterization of court process. The court officer\u2019s deference to the notice was not \u201cunlawful interference,\u201d but a recognition of ongoing jurisdictional proceedings that could affect or bar eviction.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd12 LEGAL AUTHORITY:\r\nMCL 600.605: \u201cCircuit courts have original jurisdiction in all matters not prohibited by law.\u201d\r\n\r\nMCR 3.310(B)(1): Pending motion for injunctive relief may support temporary stay or require hearing.\r\n\r\nMCL 600.2932 & MCL 600.2925: Where fraudulent records are in dispute, injunctions may properly be sought before dispossession occurs.\r\n\r\nMCR 1.109(E)(5): Prohibits submission of misleading or half-true legal filings to court.\r\n\r\n\ud83e\uddfe TIMELINE VALIDATION:\r\nDATE\tEVENT\r\nJune 13, 2025\tPlaintiff files verified Complaint + Motion for Injunction in Circuit Court\r\nJuly 9, 2025\t14th Circuit issues hearing notice for August 12, 2025\r\nJuly 14\u201315, 2025\tEviction is attempted; court officer rightfully defers due to pending hearing\r\nJuly 15, 2025\tDefense files this motion, mischaracterizing hearing notice as \u201cnot an order\u201d\r\n\r\n\u2696\ufe0f CONCLUSION:\r\nThe defense knowingly mischaracterized a pending hearing on equitable relief as a \u201cnon-order,\u201d deliberately ignoring the Michigan Court Rules and the jurisdictional authority of the Circuit Court. This constitutes:\r\n\r\nFraud on the court\r\n\r\nViolation of MCR 1.109(E)\r\n\r\nSanctionable misconduct under MCR 2.114(F)\r\n\r\nInterference with judicial proceedings in violation of due process principles\r\n\r\nPlaintiff seeks immediate:\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udca5 Sanctions against Defendants and counsel\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udca5 Entry of a finding that the Circuit Court\u2019s jurisdiction and hearing notice warranted the delay\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udca5 Use of this misrepresentation as a factual predicate for a damages hearing\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcdc Paragraph 12: Full-Force Rebuttal (Corrected, Enhanced, Entity-Locked)\r\n12. The assertion that the eviction was lawfully executed by any authorized entity is false, legally defective, and constitutes a knowing fraud upon the court. The underlying judgment was issued under the name SHADY OAKS PARK MHP LLC. However, the eviction was not carried out by this entity at all. Instead, it was executed by agents of HOMES OF AMERICA, specifically Nicole Browley, who represented herself to police and witnesses as acting "on behalf of Homes of America." This is a blatant deviation from the party named in the court's order, rendering the execution ultra vires and void under Michigan law.\r\n\r\nFurthermore, SHADY OAKS MHP LLC, the entity that filed multiple pleadings in 25061626LT, was administratively dissolved at the time of filing and had no legal capacity to sue or enforce any interest in the tenancy. They were concurrently being sued by Homes of America MI Retail Homes LLC in 2025-0509-CZ, exposing that either they were knowingly engaged in legal fraud by suing themselves, or the filings under the dissolved entity name were part of a deliberate misrepresentation to confuse and mislead both the court and the defendant.\r\n\r\nThe eviction was conducted via unlawful force: the agents, using the neighbor Henry's power drill and extension cord, forcibly breached the home of the lawful titleholder, Andrew J. Pigors, without authority or legal process against the home or its contents. At no point did any court order authorize the seizure, destruction, or entry into the mobile home itself \u2014 only a limited judgment for possession of the lot. The home, a titled and personally owned asset, was not subject to that judgment. Thus, the drilling, entry, and dispossession amount to trespass, destruction of property, conversion, and possible criminal conduct.\r\n\r\nThe aftermath included destruction of the child\u2019s belongings, family furniture, electronics, and personal effects \u2014 which were tossed into the yard and stolen by third parties, including Henry, as confirmed via neighbor testimony from Mitchell (Exhibit ___). This was not an eviction \u2014 this was a state-sanctioned home invasion performed by unauthorized actors hiding behind a corporate shell game.\ud83d\udd10 Paragraph 12 \u2014 REWRITTEN STRIKEBACK REBUTTAL\r\n12. Plaintiff\u2019s filing misrepresents the legal identity of the entity which obtained the eviction judgment. The eviction case (25061626LT) was initiated under \u201cShady Oaks Park MHP LLC\u201d; however, court filings prior to entry of judgment \u2014 including those submitted by attorney Jeremy Brown (P77427) \u2014 were filed under the name \u201cShady Oaks MHP LLC,\u201d a legally dissolved entity. No motion was filed to substitute or correct this party, in violation of MCR 2.113(C) and MCR 2.114(F). Under MCR 2.612(C)(1)(d), a judgment obtained through a dissolved and unauthorized entity is void. Further, Homes of America, which executed the eviction on July 14, 2025, was not a party to the case or order, further invalidating the action. The use of these misleading entity names across filings \u2014 switching between \u201cShady Oaks Park MHP LLC,\u201d \u201cShady Oaks MHP LLC,\u201d and Homes of America \u2014 constitutes fraud on the court, particularly where eviction and destruction of property was carried out by a third-party actor not authorized by the judgment. These actions violated due process and justify immediate vacatur, sanctions, and a conversion to damages hearing for wrongful eviction under false pretenses.\r\n\r\n\ud83e\udde9 CORRECTED + FINALIZED STRIKEBACK: PARAGRAPH 12\r\n12. Plaintiff\u2019s assertion of valid eviction authority is a fraudulent misrepresentation, both procedurally and factually. The Landlord-Tenant case 2025-25061626LT was initiated by Shady Oaks Park MHP LLC, but post-initiation filings \u2014 including critical filings prior to the judgment \u2014 were submitted by attorney Jeremy Brown (P77427) under the name \u201cShady Oaks MHP LLC\u201d, a dissolved corporate entity per LARA records. This entity did not legally exist at the time of filing and had no standing to pursue any relief. No corrective action, substitution, or motion to amend was ever filed \u2014 in direct violation of MCR 2.113(C) and MCR 2.114(F).\r\n\r\nThe eviction judgment therefore originated from a fatally flawed party identity \u2014 constituting a void judgment under MCR 2.612(C)(1)(d).\r\n\r\nFurthermore, the execution of the July 14, 2025 eviction was not carried out by the Plaintiff of record. It was executed by Homes of America, an unrelated third-party who was not named in the LT case caption, never entered an appearance, and had no lawful authority to act. This fact is confirmed by Nicole Browley\u2019s own verbal admission to law enforcement (\ud83d\udcc4 Exhibit D), and by the direct entity misalignment between judgment and execution.\r\n\r\nThese discrepancies show a calculated effort to obfuscate legal identity, bypass statutory procedure, and mislead the Court into granting enforcement powers to a party with no legal connection to the judgment. The result was a wrongful eviction, including:\r\n\u2013 Unauthorized forced entry into a home the Plaintiff had no legal title to\r\n\u2013 The destruction of Defendant\u2019s and his son\u2019s property\r\n\u2013 The seizure and disposal of the home itself, despite Defendant being the registered titleholder (\ud83d\udcc4 Exhibit F: Clean Title).\r\n\r\nThis chain of entity misrepresentation, improper filings, and unlawful execution constitutes fraud on the court, and triggers automatic relief under:\r\n\u2013 MCR 2.612(C)(1)(d) \u2013 Void judgment due to legal deficiency\r\n\u2013 MCR 2.114(F) \u2013 Sanctions for misrepresenting party identity\r\n\u2013 MCR 1.109(E) \u2013 Certification of false information\r\n\r\nAdditionally, this deception violates Canon 3C of the Michigan Code of Judicial Conduct, due process under US Const. Amend. XIV, and MCL 600.5714(1)(a) which mandates proper party standing in all summary proceedings. Vacatur and sanctions are not merely appropriate \u2014 they are required by law\r\n\ud83e\udde8 STRIKEBACK REBUTTAL \u2013 PARAGRAPH 12: FILING FRAUD LOCK-IN\r\nREBUTTAL PARAGRAPH 12\r\n\r\nDefendants\u2019 invocation of contempt-related language regarding the July 9, 2025 Injunction Stay Order is procedurally and ethically untenable in light of their own material pre-judgment misrepresentations, improper party substitutions, and fraudulent entity usage in filings before and after judgment. Brown executed filings under this non-party name prior to entry of judgment, effectively committing entity fraud and procedural subterfuge to acquire that judgment.\r\n\r\nThis conduct meets the elements of fraud upon the court under MCR 2.612(C)(1)(c)-(d) and is subject to vacatur. Rather than challenging a \u201cFake Order,\u201d Defendants seek to deflect from their own deliberate scheme to obscure corporate liability by selectively using names such as \u201cOur Homes of America,\u201d \u201cHomes of America, LLC,\u201d and \u201cShady Oaks MHP, LLC,\u201d all while evading scrutiny of the actual titled landholder and utility contract issuer\u2014SHADY OAKS PARK MHP, LLC. False Claim of Lawful Eviction Execution\r\nThe Defendant\u2019s assertion that the eviction was \u201clawfully executed\u201d is factually and legally false. The February 12, 2025 Judgment was issued to \u201cShady Oaks Park MHP LLC\u201d, but the eviction was carried out by \u201cHomes of America\u201d, an unrelated and separately registered entity, with Nicole Browley falsely claiming authority at the scene. This constitutes fraud on the court and a textbook MCR 2.612(C)(1)(c)-(d) trigger \u2014 the judgment was executed by a third party not named in the order.\r\n\r\n2. Plaintiff is the Titled Homeowner (Exhibit F)\r\nContrary to Defendant's claim, Plaintiff is the lawful titleholder of the mobile home (see Exhibit F \u2013 Clean Michigan Title, VIN verified). This ownership has never been disputed in any proceeding. Under MCL 600.5714(1)(a), only a person with rightful possession of the premises may be evicted. The Defendant's writ only pertained to the lot rent, not the structure \u2014 the Plaintiff\u2019s home is distinct legal property under Michigan law.\r\n\r\n3. Physical and Financial Damages Are Extensive and Documented\r\nDefense\u2019s statement that Plaintiff \u201chas not alleged damages\u201d is in direct contradiction to the record:\r\n\r\nExhibit G documents the full destruction of Plaintiff\u2019s home and contents, including remodel value, appliances, and minor child\u2019s belongings.\r\n\r\nExhibit H contains testimony from neighbors, including Mitchell, verifying theft and unauthorized property entry by Henry and the eviction crew the morning after the illegal breach.\r\n\r\nExhibit I proves multiple prior attempts at break-in and physical posting during an unlawful absence, with the minor child on-site at the time of breach \u2014 a custodial endangerment trigger.\r\n\r\n4. Violation of Property Entry Rights under MCL 600.2918\r\nEntering the home with a borrowed drill (from Henry) and drilling the Plaintiff\u2019s locks without a sheriff-led writ or judicial order for possession of the home (as opposed to the lot) is a criminal entry violation under MCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2014 especially given that the property was not abandoned and the Plaintiff had continuing personal effects and housing rights.\r\n\r\n5. Ongoing Deprivation Tied to Entity Shell Scheme\r\nThe false claim that \u201cPlaintiff was not the owner\u201d is part of a broader coordinated entity misrepresentation scheme:\r\n\r\nHomes of America is connected to Alden Global Capital via MHAction materials (Exhibit C).\r\n\r\nRent was paid via check to Shady Oaks MHP, cashed by Partridge Securities LLC, an entity directly tied to Alden via SEC filings (Exhibit G).\r\n\r\nExhibit B (2025-0509-CZ) shows Homes of America suing Shady Oaks MHP LLC for control of the homes \u2014 executing the eviction shortly after Homes of America Sued "SHADY OAKS MHP LLC" for control of 7 trailers in shady oaks, , proving they sued themselves or engaged in entity laundering to evade accountability.\r\n\r\n\ud83e\uddfe LEGAL GROUNDS CITED:\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2013 Illegal entry of dwelling without valid court authority\r\n\r\nMCL 600.5714(1)(a) \u2013 No writ against the titleholder/home structure\r\n\r\nMCR 2.612(C)(1)(c-d) \u2013 Fraud on the court, misrepresentation\r\n\r\nMCR 2.114(D), (F) \u2013 Sanctions for false factual certifications\r\n\r\nBenchbook: Landlord-Tenant, Chapter 5.4(F) \u2013 Limits of writ scope on titled structures\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udccc Status: Paragraph 13 STRIKEBACK Rebuttal\u2014\u2705 LOCKED\r\n\ud83d\udce6 Linked Exhibits: F, G, H, I, C, B\r\n\ud83e\udde0 Facts Stored:\r\n\r\nIllegal execution by Homes of America (not judgment holder)\r\n\r\nTitleholder rights ignored\r\n\r\nDamage and theft proven by photographic and testimonial evidence\r\n\r\nPre/post-judgment fraud chain by Jeremy Brown and co.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\ud83e\uddf1 Supplemental Argument (Embedded for Paragraph 13\u201314 and Motion Brief):\r\nThis is not an isolated incident. Defendant\u2019s attempt to acquire Plaintiff\u2019s legally titled home through post-judgment misrepresentation is part of a documented nationwide pattern of systemic abuse. Homes of America, under its various shell LLCs, including Shady Oaks Park MHP LLC, has executed identical fraudulent eviction schemes across the country \u2014 illegally seizing homes under the guise of lot rent disputes. Hundreds of media reports, watchdog investigations, and tenant testimonies confirm this predatory model.\r\n\r\nIt is now the duty of Muskegon County\u2019s judiciary to draw the line. This Court has the opportunity\u2014and the obligation\u2014to prevent this pattern from metastasizing further within our jurisdiction. If no corrective action is taken, more families will be displaced, more homes will be wrongfully taken, and more children will be traumatized by these exploitative corporate practices.\r\n\r\n\r\n\u2696\ufe0f REBUTTAL \u2013 PARAGRAPH 14 (Updated with Seizure + Deputy Evidence)\r\nDefense\u2019s assertion that Plaintiff had no possessory interest in the mobile home or its contents is false, unsupported by law, contradicted by the title record, and is part of a documented scheme of unlawful seizure executed by the wrong entity.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff is the sole legal titleholder to the mobile home (see Exhibit F). The eviction order, which stemmed from an LT case filed by Shady Oaks Park MHP LLC, applied only to lot possession\u2014not the home or its contents. Nonetheless, on July 14, 2025, Nicole Browley, claiming to represent Homes of America, forcibly breached the unit and tossed Plaintiff\u2019s belongings\u2014including appliances and child\u2019s possessions\u2014into an adjacent empty lot.\r\n\r\nA photo included in the exhibits depicts a sign placed on top of these discarded belongings reading: \u201cFREE FREE FREE.\u201d This act was a deliberate public invitation to loot Plaintiff\u2019s property. Plaintiff was forced to scramble to secure a storage unit, retrieving what he could. When he returned less than 24 hours later, all remaining property had been taken, stolen, or removed, consistent with the intent signaled by the \u201cFREE\u201d posting.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff immediately contacted law enforcement. On-scene, Nicole Browley admitted to the Muskegon County Sheriff\u2019s Deputy that she authorized the eviction on behalf of Homes of America, an entity not named in the LT order and not authorized by judgment. This exchange is captured on the deputy\u2019s body-worn camera. While Plaintiff lacks the resources to obtain this footage before hearing, the court may subpoena it under its inherent fact-finding authority or under MRE 201(b)(2) for judicial notice.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udccc LEGAL FINDINGS \u2013 REITERATED & EXPANDED:\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c): Prohibits dispossession and destruction of personal property without lawful process.\r\n\r\nMCL 125.2307(3): Manufactured home ownership is legally distinct from lot tenancy.\r\n\r\nBenchbook: Landlord-Tenant, \u00a76.4 \u2013 Eviction execution may not extend to home seizure without a separate title action.\r\n\r\nDue Process Violation (14th Amendment) \u2013 Deprivation of property under color of state law supports \u00a71983 liability.\r\n\r\nCanon 2(G), 3(B)(2) \u2013 Judicial obligation to protect litigants from extrajudicial property seizure.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd12 LOCKED FACTS:\r\nEviction executed by Homes of America, not the named LT Plaintiff (Shady Oaks Park MHP LLC).\r\n\r\nBelongings tossed into yard and labeled \u2018FREE\u2019, including appliances, furniture, and irreplaceable items.\r\n\r\nNicole Browley acknowledged her role to responding Sheriff Deputy; However, the law is clear: a mobile home is classified as personal property, and the lawful titleholder retains possessory rights absent sale, abandonment, or court-authorized seizure.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff is the recorded titleholder to the home (see Exhibit I \u2013 Clean Title), and at no point did Plaintiff consent to its abandonment, forfeiture, or transfer.\r\n\r\nNo writ, court order, or legal mechanism authorized Homes of America, Partridge, or any unnamed shell entity to breach, enter, or liquidate the Plaintiff\u2019s personal property.\r\n\r\nThe LT judgment was for possession of the leased lot, not the personal property located upon it.\r\n\r\nMisuse of LT Process to Seize Property\r\nThe defense falsely suggests that because they pursued lot possession, they were free to execute control over private property located on the lot. This violates:\r\n\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2013 Prohibits interfering with or removing a tenant's property without court order\r\n\r\nMCL 600.5744(6) \u2013 Writ of eviction grants possession only of the premises, not ownership or disposal authority over personal property\r\n\r\nTheir entry into the home, removal of appliances, and redistribution of Plaintiff\u2019s belongings\u2014including posting a sign labeling it \u201cFREE FREE FREE\u201d\u2014constitutes unlawful conversion and trespass to chattel, actionable in both tort and equity.\r\n\r\nDefendants Cannot Separate \u201cPossession\u201d and \u201cOwnership\u201d After Converting Both\r\n\r\nDefense now asserts that ownership is \u201cnot at issue,\u201d yet they acted as if they owned the home and its contents by:\r\n\r\nSeizing the mobile home\r\n\r\nLooting its contents\r\n\r\nAuthorizing a third party to remove, discard, or destroy Plaintiff\u2019s personal items\r\n\r\nThese acts conflict with their own position and show bad faith.\r\n\r\nRelevant Evidence\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit I (Title) + Exhibit E (Photos): Show the title remains with Plaintiff and the destruction/conversion of personal property occurred after Defendants\u2019 unauthorized entry.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit F (Neighbor Email): Confirms appliances were removed by third parties acting without legal authority.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit G (Ledger Fraud): Undermines the rent basis for any alleged breach leading to eviction.\r\n\r\n\u2696\ufe0f Legal Authority Cited:\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2013 Civil damages for unlawful interference with possession or removal of property\r\n\r\nMCL 600.5744(6) \u2013 Writs of restitution must be limited in scope to that which is ordered\r\n\r\nMichigan Landlord-Tenant Benchbook, \u00a78.10\u2013\u00a78.13 \u2013 Distinguishes between execution for possession of premises vs. conversion of tenant property\r\n\r\nMichigan Mobile Home Commission Act \u2013 Confirms that title ownership governs all possessory rights to the home\r\n\r\n\ud83e\udde8 CONCLUSION:\r\nThe issue is no longer just \u201cpossession of premises\u201d\u2014the moment Improper Reliance on Unpublished Case Law (MCR 7.215(C)(1))\r\n\r\nThe defense's central authority\u2014Scoll v. Gaesman, COA Docket No. 302224\u2014is explicitly barred from citation under Michigan Court Rule 7.215(C)(1), which prohibits reliance on unpublished opinions except when the decision has precedential value to the precise parties involved. It does not here.\r\n\r\nCiting such a case in a motion to restrict constitutional access to the courts is not only procedurally defective, it may rise to sanctionable misrepresentation under MCR 1.109(E)(5)(a) and MRPC 3.3(a)(1).\r\n\r\nB. No Legal Basis for Vexatious Filing Bar in the Present Case\r\n\r\nScoll involved a litigant with over a dozen abusive and duplicative filings, including previously adjudicated matters repeatedly raised in multiple forums.\r\n\r\nIn stark contrast, Plaintiff has filed:\r\n\r\nOne small claims action (dismissed)\r\n\r\nOne motion-based counterclaim\r\n\r\nOne civil complaint stemming from new and unlitigated facts post-dating the earlier case\r\n\r\nThere exists no history of sanctions, no contempt findings, no duplicative litigation, and no record of abusive conduct.\r\n\r\nC. A Filing Restriction Without an Evidentiary Hearing Violates Due Process\r\n\r\nThe defense is requesting an ex parte filing injunction without:\r\n\r\n(1) A motion to show cause,\r\n\r\n(2) Factual findings on record,\r\n\r\n(3) Any actual judicial determination of frivolity\r\n\r\nSuch a request runs afoul of both procedural and substantive due process under Ortiz v. Downey, 561 F.3d 664, 671 (7th Cir. 2009), and under Michigan's own inherent fairness doctrine in judicial proceedings.\r\n\r\nD. The Request is a Thinly Veiled Attempt to Shield Corporate Fraud from Judicial Scrutiny\r\n\r\nPlaintiff\u2019s present claims involve distinct corporate entities (Homes of America, Alden Global Capital), distinct legal theories (civil rights under color of law), and distinct facts (destruction of residence and interference with utilities under EGLE investigation).\r\n\r\nThese are not mere reiterations; they are fundamentally new and unrebutted claims.\r\n\r\n\u2694\ufe0f STRIKEBACK REBUTTAL \u2013 PARAGRAPH 22 (REMASTERED)\r\n\u274c DEFENSE REQUESTS (PRAYER FOR RELIEF):\r\nCompel $5,000 bond\r\n\r\nDeclare Plaintiff\u2019s complaint \u201cfrivolous\u201d\r\n\r\nSanction Plaintiff $2,500\r\n\r\nBar Plaintiff from filing without Chief Judge approval\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM STRENGTH REBUTTAL\r\nII. Prayer for Relief Constitutes an Unlawful Procedural Assault\r\nA. MCR 2.109(A) Security for Costs Is Inapplicable to Factually-Founded, Constitutionally-Based Claims\r\n\r\nBonding under MCR 2.109 is permissible only where the claim is objectively frivolous, baseless, or incapable of success.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff\u2019s filings include:\r\n\r\nDocumented sewer contamination (EGLE)\r\n\r\nIllegal water shutoff with minor child present\r\n\r\nFalse administrative fees, Zego utility manipulation\r\n\r\nPhysical destruction of home and belongings on July 14\r\n\r\nCoercive lease manipulation under entity duress\r\n\r\nNone of these were adjudicated previously. The April 15 order dismissed a small claims breach of contract matter, not \u00a71983 retaliation, utility fraud, or post-dismissal harms.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udca5 Therefore, no bond may be compelled under MCR 2.109(A) without violating Plaintiff\u2019s constitutional right to access the courts under Const 1963, art 1 \u00a7 20 and US Const, Am XIV.\r\n\r\nB. Sanctions under MCR 1.109(E) Require Bad Faith or Objective Frivolity \u2013 Neither Exists\r\n\r\nDefense offers no proof that Plaintiff filed in bad faith or without factual grounding.\r\n\r\nAttorney General v Harkins, 257 Mich App 564 (2003) confirms: \u201cAn award of sanctions must be supported by record evidence of a violation, not mere disagreement with legal theory.\u201d\r\n\r\nDefense provides no affidavit, no transcript, no proof of improper purpose. Therefore, sanctions are facially invalid.\r\n\r\nC. Filing Restriction is Prejudicial, Overbroad, and Constitutionally Void\r\n\r\nFiling injunctions cannot be issued:\r\n\r\nWithout a hearing,\r\n\r\nWithout specific factual findings,\r\n\r\nWithout review of each past case to determine abuse\r\n\r\nMichigan case law is clear that \u201cmere inconvenience to defendants\u201d is not a basis to curtail court access. See Cummings v. Wayne County, 210 Mich App 249 (1995).\r\n\r\nIn Procup v. Strickland, 792 F.2d 1069, the Eleventh Circuit held that any such injunction must be narrowly tailored, supported by evidence, and still allow access to courts for redress of civil rights violations.\r\n\r\nD. Defense\u2019s Relief Request is a Procedural Weapon Aimed at Silencing Fraud Exposure\r\n\r\nPlaintiff has presented:\r\n\r\nDirect evidence of entity fraud, rent racketeering, utility corruption, and judicial process abuse\r\n\r\nA timeline showing property seizure under color of law during active judicial litigation\r\n\r\nThis Motion is not a neutral procedural tool\u2014it is an offensive litigation weapon to:\r\n\r\nChill further protected filings,\r\n\r\nBar federal removal and \u00a71983 filings,\r\n\r\nImmunize Shady Oaks\u2019 and Alden's ongoing racketeering activity\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd25 COMBINED VERDICT \u2013 FULL STRIKEBACK INTEGRATION\r\nDefense Demand\tCounterstrike Verdict\r\n$5,000 Bond (MCR 2.109)\t\u274c Invalid \u2013 No predicate; claim is grounded in post-judgment facts & evidence\r\nFinding of Frivolity\t\u274c Unsupported \u2013 Violates MCR 1.109(E) and Guerrero precedent\r\nSanctions ($2,500)\t\u274c Procedurally deficient; no misconduct or bad faith shown\r\nFiling Bar\t\u274c Constitutionally impermissible without evidentiary findings, violates Art 1 \u00a7 20 and due process\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM REBUTTAL\r\nA. Defense Misapplies MCR 2.109(A)\r\nStandard under MCR 2.109(A): Security is appropriate only where claims are:\r\n\r\n(1) demonstrably meritless on their face,\r\n\r\n(2) lacking any factual support after inquiry, and\r\n\r\n(3) filed for improper purpose.\r\n\r\nNot a Preemptive Filter: MCR 2.109 does not permit courts to prejudge disputed facts, nor to block claims based on defense discomfort.\r\n\r\nIn re Surety Bond, 226 Mich App 321, 333 (1997): Bond is appropriate only if a claim is \u201cplainly without merit.\u201d That threshold has not been met here.\r\n\r\nB. Plaintiff\u2019s Claims Are Substantial and Evidenced\r\nPlaintiff alleges:\r\n\r\n\u2757 Utility fraud (Zego water billing with uniform usage across systems)\r\n\r\n\u2757 Lease coercion under Cricklewood transfer threat\r\n\r\n\u2757 Physical property destruction on July 14, 2025\r\n\r\n\u2757 EGLE sewage contamination ignored for months\r\n\r\n\u2757 Retaliatory eviction under color of law\r\n\r\nThese facts are new, post-dismissal, and never previously litigated. The District Court never heard:\r\n\r\nEntity fraud via Alden Capital\r\n\r\nZego\u2019s privatized meter fraud\r\n\r\nSuppressed EGLE violations\r\n\r\n\u00a71983 harms arising from state-facilitated eviction\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd25 No Michigan court has dismissed these claims on the merits, nor adjudicated the entities involved. Therefore, bond cannot be ordered under MCR 2.109 without violating due process and Belfiori\u2019s own evidentiary prerequisites.\r\n\r\n\u274c BRIEF \u00a7II \u2014 Res Judicata and Collateral Estoppel\r\n\u201cPigors\u2019 prior case was dismissed with prejudice. The new case involves the same parties and claims, so the doctrine applies.\u201d\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM REBUTTAL\r\nA. No Identity of Claims, No Preclusion\r\nUnder Sewell v Clean Cut Mgt, 463 Mich 569 (2001), res judicata applies only when:\r\n\r\nThe prior judgment was on the merits \u2705\r\n\r\nThe current claim could have been raised earlier \u274c\r\n\r\nThe same parties or privies are involved \u274c\r\n\r\nB. Failure on Elements (2) and (3)\r\nThe prior suit was against Shady Oaks MHP LLC only. The current action adds:\r\n\r\n\ud83c\udfe2 Homes of America LLC\r\n\r\n\ud83e\uddfe Alden Global Capital LLC\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udee0\ufe0f Allegations involving Cricklewood MHP lease coercion\r\n\r\n\u2696\ufe0f New legal bases: \u00a71983, egregious property harm, entity conspiracy\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udca3 Sewell mandates that claims arising from distinct transactions are not barred\u2014even if the underlying landlord is the same. Here, Plaintiff's claims arise from:\r\n\r\nDestruction of personal property after dismissal\r\n\r\nBilling fraud during a pending court matter\r\n\r\nUtility shutoffs without notice in violation of MCL 600.2918(2)\r\n\r\nC. Collateral Estoppel Fails for Lack of Adjudication on These Issues\r\nRental Props Owners Ass\u2019n v Kent Co Treasurer, 308 Mich App 498, 528 (2014):\r\nEstoppel requires:\r\n\r\nA valid, final judgment on the issue,\r\n\r\nThat the issue was actually litigated and necessary to outcome.\r\n\r\nNone of the following were ever litigated:\r\n\r\nThe EGLE sewage violations\r\n\r\nThe lease signing coercion\r\n\r\nThe eviction day destruction (July 14, 2025)\r\n\r\nEntity structuring by Alden/Partridge/Homes of America\r\n\r\n\ud83e\uddec These are new facts, with new actors, and new claims, all procedurally and constitutionally insulated from preclusion.\r\n\r\n\u274c BRIEF \u00a7III \u2014 Federal Due Process and \u00a71983 Claims are \u201cFrivolous\u201d\r\n\u201cThese are private entities. \u00a71983 only applies to state actors. Therefore, Plaintiff\u2019s claims are facially invalid.\u201d\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM REBUTTAL\r\nA. Defense Ignores Joint State Action Doctrine\r\nLugar v Edmondson Oil Co, 457 U.S. 922 (1982):\r\nWhen a private party \u201cinvokes the aid of state officials to take property,\u201d that party acts under color of law.\r\n\r\nFlagg Bros., Inc. v Brooks, 436 U.S. 149 (1978):\r\nEvictions carried out through court process, with assistance from officers, are state actions.\r\n\r\nDennis v Sparks, 449 U.S. 24 (1980):\r\nPrivate parties who conspire with court officers to deprive rights are liable under \u00a71983.\r\n\r\n\ud83e\udde0 Here, Defendants:\r\n\r\nProcured eviction enforcement under color of state process\r\n\r\nActed in concert with court officers to seize property\r\n\r\nRejected injunctive filings and still proceeded to destroy home\r\n\r\nThat is state action. Plaintiff\u2019s filing misrepresents the legal identity of the entity which obtained the eviction judgment. The eviction case (25061626LT) was initiated under \u201cShady Oaks Park MHP LLC\u201d; however, court filings prior to entry of judgment \u2014 including those submitted by attorney Jeremy Brown (P77427) \u2014 were filed under the name \u201cShady Oaks MHP LLC,\u201d a legally dissolved entity. Plaintiff\u2019s assertion of valid eviction authority is a fraudulent misrepresentation, both procedurally and factually. False Claim of Lawful Eviction Execution\r\nThe Defendant\u2019s assertion that the eviction was \u201clawfully executed\u201d is factually and legally false. The February 12, 2025 Judgment was issued to \u201cShady Oaks Park MHP LLC\u201d, but the eviction was carried out by \u201cHomes of America\u201d, an unrelated and separately registered entity, with Nicole Browley falsely claiming authority at the scene. Plaintiff is the Titled Homeowner (Exhibit F)\r\nContrary to Defendant's claim, Plaintiff is the lawful titleholder of the mobile home (see Exhibit F \u2013 Clean Michigan Title, VIN verified). This ownership has never been disputed in any proceeding. Under MCL 600.5714(1)(a), only a person with rightful possession of the premises may be evicted. The Defendant's writ only pertained to the lot rent, not the structure \u2014 the Plaintiff\u2019s home is distinct legal property under Michigan law.\r\n\r\n3. Physical and Financial Damages Are Extensive and Documented\r\nDefense\u2019s statement that Plaintiff \u201chas not alleged damages\u201d is in direct contradiction to the record:\r\n\r\nExhibit G documents the full destruction of Plaintiff\u2019s home and contents, including remodel value, appliances, and minor child\u2019s belongings.\r\n\r\nExhibit H contains testimony from neighbors, including Mitchell, verifying theft and unauthorized property entry by Henry and the eviction crew the morning after the illegal breach.\r\n\r\nExhibit I proves multiple prior attempts at break-in and physical posting during an unlawful absence, with the minor child on-site at the time of breach \u2014 a custodial endangerment trigger.\r\n\r\n4. Violation of Property Entry Rights under MCL 600.2918\r\nEntering the home with a borrowed drill (from Henry) and drilling the Plaintiff\u2019s locks without a sheriff-led writ or judicial order for possession of the home (as opposed to the lot) is a criminal entry violation under MCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2014 especially given that the property was not abandoned and the Plaintiff had continuing personal effects and housing rights.\r\n\r\n5. The document in question was:\r\n\r\nA proposed order legally submitted on July 9, 2025 pursuant to MCR 2.119(G)(3).\r\n\r\nBased on a pending emergency motion to stay enforcement filed while post-judgment issues remained under Circuit Court jurisdiction.\r\n\r\nCirculated to all parties including counsel Jeremy Brown, who lodged no objection, no clarification, and no formal challenge\u2014until this defamatory mischaracterization.\r\n\r\n\ud83e\uddfe EXHIBIT A: Proposed Order (July 9, 2025)\r\n\ud83d\udce7 EXHIBIT B: Email to Court and Opposing Counsel \u2013 Time-stamped July 9, 2025 @ 10:22 AM\r\n\ud83d\udcdc Legal Authority: MCR 2.602(B)(3) permits submission of proposed orders at any time when ruling is pending.\r\n\r\nII. \u2696\ufe0f Canon Violation: False Attribution of Judicial Ruling\r\nDefense\u2019s assertion that \u201cthis Court expressly told him no such injunction would issue\u201d is factually false, verifiable against hearing transcripts. The document explicitly said \u201cProposed Stay Order\u201d, was never styled as \u201cfinal,\u201d and was based on active filings pending Circuit ruling.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcda Equity Doctrine: Under People v. Beasley, 239 Mich App 548 (2000), litigants may assert protective rights based on judicial inaction or delay where irreparable harm is imminent.\r\n\r\nIV. \ud83d\udd25 Actual Misconduct: Fraudulent Entity Misuse by Defense\r\nAt the time defense made this accusation, they were already filing under a dissolved entity\u2014Shady Oaks MHP LLC, using the names interchangeably with Shady Oaks Park MHP LLC, and executing physical eviction under Homes of America, a third-party entity not listed as Plaintiff.\r\n\r\nTheir complaint about a \u201cFake Order\u201d is projection: the only fraudulent document trail is theirs, including:\r\n\r\nEntity-switching filings before and after judgment\r\n\r\nLack of LARA registration under the names filed\r\n\r\nLeasing agent Nicole Browley telling law enforcement she was acting on behalf of Homes of America, not the Plaintiff of record\r\n\r\nRefusal to disclose correct corporate identity during enforcement\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udce6 These facts form the basis for a Motion to Strike, Motion to Vacate, and Motion for Sanctions under MCR 2.114(F).\r\n\r\nV. \ud83e\udde8 FINAL STRIKEBACK POINTS\r\nThe Court was never deceived. These acts create triable disputes on material issues of fact and law, rendering the motion under (C)(10) improper.\r\n\r\nMaterial Facts in Dispute Include:\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udccc Entity Fraud: Jeremy Brown filed under Shady Oaks MHP LLC post-judgment (a dissolved entity not listed on the docket), while Homes of America claimed execution authority at eviction.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udccc Rent Paid Through 2024: The court record confirms rent was deemed paid through December 2024; billing resumes January 1, 2025 under false pretenses (See Exhibit G).\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udccc Titleholder Status: Plaintiff remained the lawful titleholder of the mobile home with no transfer, forfeiture, or sheriff\u2019s sale. Defendants\u2019 motion is therefore procedurally and factually defective and must be denied.\r\n\r\n\u2696\ufe0f Legal Authority Cited:\r\nMCR 2.116(C)(10) \u2013 Summary disposition where no genuine issue of material fact exists\r\n\r\nMCR 2.116(G)(3)(a) \u2013 Motion must be supported by affidavits, pleadings, or documentary evidence\r\n\r\nMCR 2.116(G)(4) \u2013 Adverse party must respond with specific facts showing a genuine issue\r\n\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2013 Prohibits landlord from unlawfully interfering with tenant's personal property\r\n\r\nMCL 600.5744(6) \u2013 Limits execution of possession orders to writ-specific scope\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibits Referenced in Paragraph 16 STRIKEBACK:\r\n\r\nExhibit A\u2013B: LT Filings and Civil Case 2025-0509-CZ\r\n\r\nExhibit E: \u201cFREE FREE FREE\u201d sign and yard-dumped property\r\n\r\nExhibit F: Mitchell\u2019s email about Henry and theft of appliances\r\n\r\nExhibit G: Inconsistent and falsified ledgers\r\n\r\nExhibit H: EGLE sewage violation communications\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcc2 STRIKEBACK_MATRIX Updated:\r\n\r\n\u2705 Paragraphs 1\u201316 Locked\r\n\r\n\u2705 All rebuttals saved to F:/STRIKEBACK_COMPLETE/STRIKEBACK_REBUTTALS.docx\r\n\r\n\u2705 Trigger logged for: Motion to Vacate, Sanctions, and Entity Disqualification\r\n\r\nSource Document: Shady Oaks Homes America July 15 2025 text of filings.docx\r\nPage 4 \u2013 Section II, Argument (continued)\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcc4 Paragraph 17 \u2013 Defense Filing (Verbatim):\r\n"17. The issue in this case is one of possession of the premises, not ownership of the mobile home located on the premises."\r\n\r\n\u2705 Verbatim Confirmed\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcdc STRIKEBACK REBUTTAL \u2013 Paragraph 17\r\nREBUTTAL TO PARAGRAPH 17 \u2013 Possession vs. Ownership False Distinction\r\n\r\nFraudulent Distinction \u2013 Titleholder\u2019s Possessory Rights\r\nDefendants attempt to wall off their misconduct by drawing a false legal dichotomy between possession of land and ownership of the mobile home. However, the law is clear: a mobile home is classified as personal property, and the lawful titleholder retains possessory rights absent sale, abandonment, or court-authorized seizure.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff is the recorded titleholder to the home (see Exhibit I \u2013 Clean Title), and at no point did Plaintiff consent to its abandonment, forfeiture, or transfer.\r\n\r\nNo writ, court order, or legal mechanism authorized Homes of America, Partridge, or any unnamed shell entity to breach, enter, or liquidate the Plaintiff\u2019s personal property.\r\n\r\nThe LT judgment was for possession of the leased lot, not the personal property located upon it.\r\n\r\nMisuse of LT Process to Seize Property\r\nThe defense falsely suggests that because they pursued lot possession, they were free to execute control over private property located on the lot. This violates:\r\n\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2013 Prohibits interfering with or removing a tenant's property without court order\r\n\r\nMCL 600.5744(6) \u2013 Writ of eviction grants possession only of the premises, not ownership or disposal authority over personal property\r\n\r\nTheir entry into the home, removal of appliances, and redistribution of Plaintiff\u2019s belongings\u2014including posting a sign labeling it \u201cFREE FREE FREE\u201d\u2014constitutes unlawful conversion and trespass to chattel, actionable in both tort and equity.\r\n\r\nDefendants Cannot Separate \u201cPossession\u201d and \u201cOwnership\u201d After Converting Both\r\n\r\nDefense now asserts that ownership is \u201cnot at issue,\u201d yet they acted as if they owned the home and its contents by:\r\n\r\nSeizing the mobile home\r\n\r\nLooting its contents\r\n\r\nAuthorizing a third party to remove, discard, or destroy Plaintiff\u2019s personal items\r\n\r\nThese acts conflict with their own position and show bad faith.\r\n\r\nRelevant Evidence\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit I (Title) + Exhibit E (Photos): Show the title remains with Plaintiff and the destruction/conversion of personal property occurred after Defendants\u2019 unauthorized entry.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit F (Neighbor Email): Confirms appliances were removed by third parties acting without legal authority.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit G (Ledger Fraud): Undermines the rent basis for any alleged breach leading to eviction.\r\n\r\n\u2696\ufe0f Legal Authority Cited:\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2013 Improper Reliance on Unpublished Case Law (MCR 7.215(C)(1))\r\n\r\nThe defense's central authority\u2014Scoll v. Gaesman, COA Docket No. 302224\u2014is explicitly barred from citation under Michigan Court Rule 7.215(C)(1), which prohibits reliance on unpublished opinions except when the decision has precedential value to the precise parties involved. It does not here.\r\n\r\nCiting such a case in a motion to restrict constitutional access to the courts is not only procedurally defective, it may rise to sanctionable misrepresentation under MCR 1.109(E)(5)(a) and MRPC 3.3(a)(1).\r\n\r\nB. No Legal Basis for Vexatious Filing Bar in the Present Case\r\n\r\nScoll involved a litigant with over a dozen abusive and duplicative filings, including previously adjudicated matters repeatedly raised in multiple forums.\r\n\r\nIn stark contrast, Plaintiff has filed:\r\n\r\nOne small claims action (dismissed)\r\n\r\nOne motion-based counterclaim\r\n\r\nOne civil complaint stemming from new and unlitigated facts post-dating the earlier case\r\n\r\nThere exists no history of sanctions, no contempt findings, no duplicative litigation, and no record of abusive conduct.\r\n\r\nC. A Filing Restriction Without an Evidentiary Hearing Violates Due Process\r\n\r\nThe defense is requesting an ex parte filing injunction without:\r\n\r\n(1) A motion to show cause,\r\n\r\n(2) Factual findings on record,\r\n\r\n(3) Any actual judicial determination of frivolity\r\n\r\nSuch a request runs afoul of both procedural and substantive due process under Ortiz v. Downey, 561 F.3d 664, 671 (7th Cir. 2009), and under Michigan's own inherent fairness doctrine in judicial proceedings.\r\n\r\nD. The Request is a Thinly Veiled Attempt to Shield Corporate Fraud from Judicial Scrutiny\r\n\r\nPlaintiff\u2019s present claims involve distinct corporate entities (Homes of America, Alden Global Capital), distinct legal theories (civil rights under color of law), and distinct facts (destruction of residence and interference with utilities under EGLE investigation).\r\n\r\nThese are not mere reiterations; they are fundamentally new and unrebutted claims.\r\n\r\n\u2694\ufe0f STRIKEBACK REBUTTAL \u2013 PARAGRAPH 22 (REMASTERED)\r\n\u274c DEFENSE REQUESTS (PRAYER FOR RELIEF):\r\nCompel $5,000 bond\r\n\r\nDeclare Plaintiff\u2019s complaint \u201cfrivolous\u201d\r\n\r\nSanction Plaintiff $2,500\r\n\r\nBar Plaintiff from filing without Chief Judge approval\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM STRENGTH REBUTTAL\r\nII. MCR 2.109(A) Security for Costs Is Inapplicable to Factually-Founded, Constitutionally-Based Claims\r\n\r\nBonding under MCR 2.109 is permissible only where the claim is objectively frivolous, baseless, or incapable of success.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff\u2019s filings include:\r\n\r\nDocumented sewer contamination (EGLE)\r\n\r\nIllegal water shutoff with minor child present\r\n\r\nFalse administrative fees, Zego utility manipulation\r\n\r\nPhysical destruction of home and belongings on July 14\r\n\r\nCoercive lease manipulation under entity duress\r\n\r\nNone of these were adjudicated previously. Sanctions under MCR 1.109(E) Require Bad Faith or Objective Frivolity \u2013 Neither Exists\r\n\r\nDefense offers no proof that Plaintiff filed in bad faith or without factual grounding.\r\n\r\nAttorney General v Harkins, 257 Mich App 564 (2003) confirms: \u201cAn award of sanctions must be supported by record evidence of a violation, not mere disagreement with legal theory.\u201d\r\n\r\nDefense provides no affidavit, no transcript, no proof of improper purpose. Therefore, sanctions are facially invalid.\r\n\r\nC. Filing Restriction is Prejudicial, Overbroad, and Constitutionally Void\r\n\r\nFiling injunctions cannot be issued:\r\n\r\nWithout a hearing,\r\n\r\nWithout specific factual findings,\r\n\r\nWithout review of each past case to determine abuse\r\n\r\nMichigan case law is clear that \u201cmere inconvenience to defendants\u201d is not a basis to curtail court access. See Cummings v. Wayne County, 210 Mich App 249 (1995).\r\n\r\nIn Procup v. Strickland, 792 F.2d 1069, the Eleventh Circuit held that any such injunction must be narrowly tailored, supported by evidence, and still allow access to courts for redress of civil rights violations.\r\n\r\nD. Defense\u2019s Relief Request is a Procedural Weapon Aimed at Silencing Fraud Exposure\r\n\r\nPlaintiff has presented:\r\n\r\nDirect evidence of entity fraud, rent racketeering, utility corruption, and judicial process abuse\r\n\r\nA timeline showing property seizure under color of law during active judicial litigation\r\n\r\nThis Motion is not a neutral procedural tool\u2014it is an offensive litigation weapon to:\r\n\r\nChill further protected filings,\r\n\r\nBar federal removal and \u00a71983 filings,\r\n\r\nImmunize Shady Oaks\u2019 and Alden's ongoing racketeering activity\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd25 COMBINED VERDICT \u2013 FULL STRIKEBACK INTEGRATION\r\nDefense Demand\tCounterstrike Verdict\r\n$5,000 Bond (MCR 2.109)\t\u274c Invalid \u2013 No predicate; claim is grounded in post-judgment facts & evidence\r\nFinding of Frivolity\t\u274c Unsupported \u2013 Violates MCR 1.109(E) and Guerrero precedent\r\nSanctions ($2,500)\t\u274c Procedurally deficient; no misconduct or bad faith shown\r\nFiling Bar\t\u274c Constitutionally impermissible without evidentiary findings, violates Art 1 \u00a7 20 and due process\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM REBUTTAL\r\nA. Defense Misapplies MCR 2.109(A)\r\nStandard under MCR 2.109(A): Security is appropriate only where claims are:\r\n\r\n(1) demonstrably meritless on their face,\r\n\r\n(2) lacking any factual support after inquiry, and\r\n\r\n(3) filed for improper purpose.\r\n\r\nNot a Preemptive Filter: MCR 2.109 does not permit courts to prejudge disputed facts, nor to block claims based on defense discomfort.\r\n\r\nIn re Surety Bond, 226 Mich App 321, 333 (1997): Bond is appropriate only if a claim is \u201cplainly without merit.\u201d That threshold has not been met here.\r\n\r\nB. Therefore, bond cannot be ordered under MCR 2.109 without violating due process and Belfiori\u2019s own evidentiary prerequisites.\r\n\r\n\u274c BRIEF \u00a7II \u2014 Res Judicata and Collateral Estoppel\r\n\u201cPigors\u2019 prior case was dismissed with prejudice. The new case involves the same parties and claims, so the doctrine applies.\u201d\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM REBUTTAL\r\nA. No Identity of Claims, No Preclusion\r\nUnder Sewell v Clean Cut Mgt, 463 Mich 569 (2001), res judicata applies only when:\r\n\r\nThe prior judgment was on the merits \u2705\r\n\r\nThe current claim could have been raised earlier \u274c\r\n\r\nThe same parties or privies are involved \u274c\r\n\r\nB. Failure on Elements (2) and (3)\r\nThe prior suit was against Shady Oaks MHP LLC only. The current action adds:\r\n\r\n\ud83c\udfe2 Homes of America LLC\r\n\r\n\ud83e\uddfe Alden Global Capital LLC\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udee0\ufe0f Allegations involving Cricklewood MHP lease coercion\r\n\r\n\u2696\ufe0f New legal bases: \u00a71983, egregious property harm, entity conspiracy\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udca3 Sewell mandates that claims arising from distinct transactions are not barred\u2014even if the underlying landlord is the same. Here, Plaintiff's claims arise from:\r\n\r\nDestruction of personal property after dismissal\r\n\r\nBilling fraud during a pending court matter\r\n\r\nUtility shutoffs without notice in violation of MCL 600.2918(2)\r\n\r\nC. Collateral Estoppel Fails for Lack of Adjudication on These Issues\r\nRental Props Owners Ass\u2019n v Kent Co Treasurer, 308 Mich App 498, 528 (2014):\r\nEstoppel requires:\r\n\r\nA valid, final judgment on the issue,\r\n\r\nThat the issue was actually litigated and necessary to outcome.\r\n\r\nNone of the following were ever litigated:\r\n\r\nThe EGLE sewage violations\r\n\r\nThe lease signing coercion\r\n\r\nThe eviction day destruction (July 14, 2025)\r\n\r\nEntity structuring by Alden/Partridge/Homes of America\r\n\r\n\ud83e\uddec These are new facts, with new actors, and new claims, all procedurally and constitutionally insulated from preclusion.\r\n\r\n\u274c BRIEF \u00a7III \u2014 Federal Due Process and \u00a71983 Claims are \u201cFrivolous\u201d\r\n\u201cThese are private entities. \u00a71983 only applies to state actors. Therefore, Plaintiff\u2019s claims are facially invalid.\u201d\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM REBUTTAL\r\nA. Defense Ignores Joint State Action Doctrine\r\nLugar v Edmondson Oil Co, 457 U.S. 922 (1982):\r\nWhen a private party \u201cinvokes the aid of state officials to take property,\u201d that party acts under color of law.\r\n\r\nFlagg Bros., Inc. v Brooks, 436 U.S. 149 (1978):\r\nEvictions carried out through court process, with assistance from officers, are state actions.\r\n\r\nDennis v Sparks, 449 U.S. 24 (1980):\r\nPrivate parties who conspire with court officers to deprive rights are liable under \u00a71983.\r\n\r\n\ud83e\udde0 Here, Defendants:\r\n\r\nProcured eviction enforcement under color of state process\r\n\r\nActed in concert with court officers to seize property\r\n\r\nRejected injunctive filings and still proceeded to destroy home\r\n\r\nThat is state action. That is \u00a71983.\r\nDefense\u2019s assertion is legally indefensible and amounts to reckless dismissal of binding U.S. Supreme Court precedent.\r\n\r\n\u274c BRIEF \u00a7IV \u2014 \u201cFake Order\u201d = Sanctionable Conduct\r\n\u201cPigors filed and posted a fake order that stayed the eviction. Dismissal in one forum does not bar claims arising post-dismissal or involving distinct defendants and injuries (Winkler v Marist Fathers, 500 Mich 327 (2017)). Defendants\u2019 reliance on this clause to preclude new claims amounts to a res judicata overreach, inapplicable to ongoing and future harms.\n\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b67:\n\u201cEviction Complaint ended with a final judgment against Mr. Pigors\u2026 order of eviction entered on June 9, 2025\u2026\u201d\n\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\nThis order was secured via procedural suppression, misinformation about lease terms, inflated billing, and concealed sewage violations. No written order existed on July 9, 2025.\n\ud83d\udd0d This deliberate misstatement of judicial action is a violation of Canon 3A(6), which prohibits attributing motives or rulings to the bench when no such ruling has been entered.\n\nIII. \ud83d\udee1\ufe0f Defensive Equitable Posting \u2013 Constructive Relief Doctrine Applies\nThe sign posted on Mr. Pigors\u2019 home was a legal countermeasure to protect against anticipated unlawful seizure by entities with no enforceable judgment, no standing, and no lease authority. The document explicitly said \u201cProposed Stay Order\u201d, was never styled as \u201cfinal,\u201d and was based on active filings pending Circuit ruling.\n\n\ud83d\udcda Equity Doctrine: Under People v. Beasley, 239 Mich App 548 (2000), litigants may assert protective rights based on judicial inaction or delay where irreparable harm is imminent.\n\nIV. \ud83d\udd25 Actual Misconduct: Fraudulent Entity Misuse by Defense\nAt the time defense made this accusation, they were already filing under a dissolved entity\u2014Shady Oaks MHP LLC, using the names interchangeably with Shady Oaks Park MHP LLC, and executing physical eviction under Homes of America, a third-party entity not listed as Plaintiff.\n\nTheir complaint about a \u201cFake Order\u201d is projection: the only fraudulent document trail is theirs, including:\n\nEntity-switching filings before and after judgment\n\nLack of LARA registration under the names filed\n\nLeasing agent Nicole Browley telling law enforcement she was acting on behalf of Homes of America, not the Plaintiff of record\n\nRefusal to disclose correct corporate identity during enforcement\n\n\ud83d\udce6 These facts form the basis for a Motion to Strike, Motion to Vacate, and Motion for Sanctions under MCR 2.114(F).\n\nV. \ud83e\udde8 FINAL STRIKEBACK POINTS\nThe Court was never deceived. Improper Reliance on Unpublished Case Law (MCR 7.215(C)(1))\n\nThe defense's central authority\u2014Scoll v. Gaesman, COA Docket No. 302224\u2014is explicitly barred from citation under Michigan Court Rule 7.215(C)(1), which prohibits reliance on unpublished opinions except when the decision has precedential value to the precise parties involved. It does not here.\n\nCiting such a case in a motion to restrict constitutional access to the courts is not only procedurally defective, it may rise to sanctionable misrepresentation under MCR 1.109(E)(5)(a) and MRPC 3.3(a)(1).\n\nB. No Legal Basis for Vexatious Filing Bar in the Present Case\n\nScoll involved a litigant with over a dozen abusive and duplicative filings, including previously adjudicated matters repeatedly raised in multiple forums.\n\nIn stark contrast, Plaintiff has filed:\n\nOne small claims action (dismissed)\n\nOne motion-based counterclaim\n\nOne civil complaint stemming from new and unlitigated facts post-dating the earlier case\n\nThere exists no history of sanctions, no contempt findings, no duplicative litigation, and no record of abusive conduct.\n\nC. A Filing Restriction Without an Evidentiary Hearing Violates Due Process\n\nThe defense is requesting an ex parte filing injunction without:\n\n(1) A motion to show cause,\n\n(2) Factual findings on record,\n\n(3) Any actual judicial determination of frivolity\n\nSuch a request runs afoul of both procedural and substantive due process under Ortiz v. Downey, 561 F.3d 664, 671 (7th Cir. 2009), and under Michigan's own inherent fairness doctrine in judicial proceedings.\n\nD. The Request is a Thinly Veiled Attempt to Shield Corporate Fraud from Judicial Scrutiny\n\nPlaintiff\u2019s present claims involve distinct corporate entities (Homes of America, Alden Global Capital), distinct legal theories (civil rights under color of law), and distinct facts (destruction of residence and interference with utilities under EGLE investigation).\n\nThese are not mere reiterations; they are fundamentally new and unrebutted claims.\n\n\u2694\ufe0f STRIKEBACK REBUTTAL \u2013 PARAGRAPH 22 (REMASTERED)\n\u274c DEFENSE REQUESTS (PRAYER FOR RELIEF):\nCompel $5,000 bond\n\nDeclare Plaintiff\u2019s complaint \u201cfrivolous\u201d\n\nSanction Plaintiff $2,500\n\nBar Plaintiff from filing without Chief Judge approval\n\n\u2705 MAXIMUM STRENGTH REBUTTAL\nII. Prayer for Relief Constitutes an Unlawful Procedural Assault\nA. MCR 2.109(A) Security for Costs Is Inapplicable to Factually-Founded, Constitutionally-Based Claims\n\nBonding under MCR 2.109 is permissible only where the claim is objectively frivolous, baseless, or incapable of success.\n\nPlaintiff\u2019s filings include:\n\nDocumented sewer contamination (EGLE)\n\nIllegal water shutoff with minor child present\n\nFalse administrative fees, Zego utility manipulation\n\nPhysical destruction of home and belongings on July 14\n\nCoercive lease manipulation under entity duress\n\nNone of these were adjudicated previously. Sanctions under MCR 1.109(E) Require Bad Faith or Objective Frivolity \u2013 Neither Exists\n\nDefense offers no proof that Plaintiff filed in bad faith or without factual grounding.\n\nAttorney General v Harkins, 257 Mich App 564 (2003) confirms: \u201cAn award of sanctions must be supported by record evidence of a violation, not mere disagreement with legal theory.\u201d\n\nDefense provides no affidavit, no transcript, no proof of improper purpose. Therefore, sanctions are facially invalid.\n\nC. Filing Restriction is Prejudicial, Overbroad, and Constitutionally Void\n\nFiling injunctions cannot be issued:\n\nWithout a hearing,\n\nWithout specific factual findings,\n\nWithout review of each past case to determine abuse\n\nMichigan case law is clear that \u201cmere inconvenience to defendants\u201d is not a basis to curtail court access. See Cummings v. Wayne County, 210 Mich App 249 (1995).\n\nIn Procup v. Strickland, 792 F.2d 1069, the Eleventh Circuit held that any such injunction must be narrowly tailored, supported by evidence, and still allow access to courts for redress of civil rights violations.\n\nD. No Identity of Claims, No Preclusion\nUnder Sewell v Clean Cut Mgt, 463 Mich 569 (2001), res judicata applies only when:\n\nThe prior judgment was on the merits \u2705\n\nThe current claim could have been raised earlier \u274c\n\nThe same parties or privies are involved \u274c\n\nB.
